Employee Correspondence

The Boredom of an Apprentice Dear Editor:

I am a child who has not received sufficient education and also a child who is interested in literature and all sciences. However, the charm of economics is oppressing me, preventing me from developing my interests. And in the year before last, I stepped into a dark society and began to live a life far away from the light. How disappointing and painful this is!

Specialized Writings

What is Scientific Management?

— Zhang Yifan

We often hear people say that someone is very shrewd and "scientific" in their work; or that a certain organization performs well and is "scientific." But what exactly does "scientific" mean? "Scientific" means being planned, organized, working efficiently, and conforming to scientific principles. The 20th century is an era of science. Whatever we do, we should base it on scientific methods to achieve perfection. Haphazard and fatalistic approaches are completely unacceptable. Therefore, "scientific management" has been promoted by Frederick Winslow Taylor of the United States in recent decades, and subsequently adopted by the industrial circles of Britain and Germany. After the European War, Germany's Walther Rathenau, based on this method, initiated what is called "industrial rationalization," which revived the declining German industry, attracting worldwide attention. In 1927, the League of Nations held an international economic conference in Geneva and decided to adopt "industrial rationalization." As a result, "scientific management" was not only adopted by European and American countries, but also by Soviet Russia in its Five-Year Plan. At the National Industry and Commerce Conference in our country, the proposal to implement rationalization and scientific management was also included in the general assembly declaration. Mr. Wang Yunwu of the Commercial Press and Mr. Xiang Kangyuan of Kangyuan Printing and Canning Factory have also made great efforts to promote it, and their experimental results have been very good. However, what exactly is "scientific management"? "Scientific management" is not just about using scientific methods to improve management and equipment, or time and motion studies... This is just a means of "scientific management." Its true essence lies in the psychological reform of both labor and management, each recognizing their responsibility to the other, and jointly seeking the development of industry.

However, scientific management also has three meanings: ㈠ narrowly defined, limited to factories; ㈡ broadly defined, extending this method to all industries and businesses, not limited to factories; ㈢ most broadly defined, not limited to one factory or one company, but encompassing the entire industry or the national economy, under which definition it is also called "industrial rationalization."

The commonly adopted "scientific management" can be roughly divided into twelve points. Due to limited space, I cannot discuss them in detail here, but only list them in outline form as follows:

(1) Time study | Measuring the daily production capacity of employees.

(2) Motion study | Studying the basic movements of work to make them the easiest and fastest.

(3) Setting work standards | Certain employees should achieve certain results each day.

(4) Memory aids | Eliminating confusion and errors.

(5) Planning work sequences | Connecting work processes and saving costs.

(6) Conserving energy | Saving energy for more work.

(7) Standardization | Specifying product styles | Saving equipment, raw materials, and procedures.

(8) Simplification | Specifying product types | Saving equipment, raw materials, and procedures.

(9) Analyzing work | Personnel and remuneration (rationalizing wages) are appropriately allocated.

(10) Requesting equipment | Saving energy, eliminating costs, and connecting various tasks.

(11) Strict organization | Defining responsibilities and expediting administration.

(12) Adopting cost accounting | Accurate budgeting to facilitate the setting of work standards.

(13) Preparing budgets | Systematizing finances and standardizing receipts and disbursements.

(14) Conducting statistics | Comparing the gains and losses of business and providing a basis for operations.

If we can plan thoroughly and implement scientific management well, not only can work efficiency be increased, but the entire industry and the entire society will also have solutions. This is even more significant in China, because if we can produce enough for our own needs after increasing production, that would be remarkable. As for the epidemics of "overproduction" and "worker unemployment," we are not afraid of them. The results of implementing "scientific management" are listed as follows:

(1) Improved labor-management relations | Sincere cooperation.

(2) Elimination of waste | Reduced costs | Low prices.

(3) Product improvement | Improved quality | High quality.

(4) Increased production | Generous shareholder dividends | Industrial development.

(5) Increased wages | Guaranteeing workers' livelihoods | Social stability.

Our country's industries are declining, production is lagging behind, and there are no large-scale factories, so there is no talk of international trade (except for a few local products). From an international perspective, we only have small-scale enterprises. Therefore, some people say: "Scientific management" is only suitable for large-scale industries. For our small factories and shops, is it "using a sledgehammer to crack a nut"? There is no need for this "fashionable foreign product" of scientific management, and we don't need to study or adopt it. Therefore, "scientific management," which has been proven effective in European and American countries, is still rarely adopted by us, which is a very regrettable thing. If we want to revitalize industry in the future, achieve low prices and high quality, and recover our rights and interests to save the country, we must fundamentally change our attitude. I hope that industrialists with aspirations in the country will use a research attitude and a scientific spirit to experiment with "scientific management" step by step.

However, when we implement this method, there is one point that should be particularly noted: that is, "the scientific spirit should pay attention to facts." Ordinary people often misunderstand "scientific management," thinking that implementing "scientific management" means focusing solely on "mechanical" methods and ignoring matters within the scope of "personnel." Without considering the internal situation, they force it into use, which often does not work. Even in European and American countries, this situation occurred frequently during the experimental period. The reason why this method is doubted is because it is not adopted properly. We should learn from this and not repeat the same mistakes. When implementing it, we should follow the following steps:

(1) Research | Methods and environment.

(2) Education | Promotion and understanding.

(3) Pay attention to the welfare of employees.

(4) Obtain the sympathy and cooperation of employees.

(5) Gradual progress.

(6) Perseverance to the end and implementation step by step.

In this way, we can avoid repeating the mistakes of the past and succeed smoothly.

The publication of your esteemed journal makes me feel that there may be a glimmer of hope in the gray future, because the content of your journal is all about guidance for our junior staff in their service, and it can be said to be a compass for our current struggles.

Now I have a few questions that I have written down below, hoping to get a satisfactory answer.

(1) After a child enters the "door of career," what methods can be used to seek further progress in learning?

(2) Why should a junior staff member be ridiculed and despised by colleagues and even tea servers?

(3) How can one achieve the "bright path" in one's career?

(4) The steps for a career person to study science | The steps for a career person who is only interested in science but has no knowledge and is economically disadvantaged to study science.

(5) How can one fulfill the obligations of a member of the Republic of China and engage in the work of resisting Japan and saving the country?

Zhou Liangji

Editor's note: We believe that the five questions raised by Mr. Zhou Liangji are common problems felt by apprentices in the business community today and are of great value for public discussion. We will now answer the first four questions raised by Mr. Zhou as follows:

(1) After a young person enters the "door of career," there are two ways to seek further progress in learning:

(A) Be loyal to your job. Seeking progress in your job is seeking progress in learning. The most relevant learning is to fulfill your duties. Watt was only an assistant repairing instruments, but because he was unwilling to be perfunctory about the water pump that a professor gave him to repair, he eventually invented the steam engine, which changed the world. Don't underestimate your small tasks; small tasks are the starting point for great achievements. Human creation is just making a big deal out of a small matter.

(B) Time is life. Use your spare time from your job to pursue the learning you like to pursue. As long as you persevere, you will surely achieve great things. For example, if you are interested in science, you should mobilize all your spare time to attack science, without letting a trace of it go to gambling venues or dance halls. A person must play, and you can play scientific tricks. If you play properly, I guarantee it will be more interesting than playing cards, and you can play out first-class learning.

(2) Why should a junior staff member be ridiculed and despised by colleagues and even tea servers? This is because of the poison of traditional concepts. I have suggested to several gentlemen that newspapers should be run as places of learning (not traditional schools but revolutionary schools). People who serve should be treated equally, without any distinction between big and small. People like tea servers and drivers originally had excessive snobbish ideas; bullying the poor and valuing the rich, flattering the big and insulting the small, are habits they acquired in an unfortunate environment. Only revolutionary education can change them. But we individuals must also put in the effort to reflect on ourselves. Those who are willing to take a loss will never take a loss in the end. Gentle people are blessed. If you treat everyone with the attitude of an educator and a student, you probably won't make any big mistakes, right? The attitude of an educator is to recognize that people are teachable and capable of doing good, not to be fond of being a teacher. If you are fond of being a teacher, people will not accept it.

(3) There are two "bright paths" in one's career: one is equal opportunity for all professions, and this path requires education and social transformation to attack from both sides in order to break through; the other is creation and invention, and on this path, natural science is the only sun, now covered by the dark clouds of superstition, fantasy, recklessness, and nonsense. We must invite our brains and hands to clear away the dark clouds so that we can see the light of day again.

(4) The steps for a career person to study science are: first, to personally play scientific tricks; second, to personally observe natural phenomena and various man-made civilizations and pursue their reasons; third, to read science books that guide experiments, not foreign stereotypes and foreign policy essays; fourth, to ask about everything and get to the bottom of it; and fifth, to continue to work hard until old age. True learning comes from "doing." The ancients had a saying, "Without learning, there is no skill." My opinion is: "Without doing, there is no learning; without doing, there is no skill." What do you think?

I wish you effort Editor's reply

Finally, we have two points to ask readers to pay attention to:

(1) The above answers are only the results of discussions between a few of us and our friends and cannot be considered satisfactory answers. We still welcome readers to join the discussion in order to gather ideas and benefit from them.

(2) We have not answered the fifth question raised by Mr. Zhou because we feel that this question must be determined based on various objective conditions and it is difficult to give an answer casually. Therefore, we have decided to put forward this question and first ask readers to express their opinions and discuss it to a certain

Comments

Happiness in Fulfilling Responsibilities

— Gongping

The great Greek philosopher Aristotle once gave a definition of mankind, calling it: "Man is a rational animal." Since ancient times, China has also had the concept that "a man without propriety, what difference is there from beasts?" Indeed, the reason why mankind can boast of being the spirit of all things is of course because mankind is rational and knows righteousness. However, human intelligence is constantly developing forward, and in the 20th century, we have realized that what distinguishes mankind from beasts, in addition to the most precious rationality, is also a more significant feature! What is this greater feature? It is the "labor" that we are most familiar with.

The "labor" mentioned here is broadly defined, encompassing all areas of human activity. Beasts have nothing to do but eat and drink when hungry and thirsty. But humans have purposeful, continuous labor to prepare for a rainy day. To know the greatness and importance of labor, we only need to observe the things we humans need at any time and place, and there is no one that does not involve our labor. Anything! Whether it is clothing, food, utensils, or works of art and literature丨the more exquisite and superb, the more difficult and time-consuming its creation must be, that is, it requires more labor. Therefore, to examine the level of culture of a country and its people, we only need to look at the development of its industry, commerce, literature, and art. Europe, America, and our enemy Japan have more developed industry, commerce, literature, and art than China, so their cultural levels are higher than China. From this, we can know how precious "labor" is to us humans. Therefore, if we want our motherland to be able to compete with Europe, America, and Japan, we can only devote ourselves to our respective careers, work hard, improve day by day, and strive for perfection in order to achieve our goal!

Humans must labor, and only labor, can they survive indefinitely. If you don't work, you die. If an individual doesn't work, the individual dies. If a nation doesn't work, that nation will surely perish. Those who enjoy ready-made things without working are the traitors of mankind. We don't have to envy them. We should boast to them with the sweat we shed. Because labor is a responsibility that everyone must fulfill!

Since labor is a responsibility that everyone should fulfill, then why do we often hear people who are working complaining about life and hating labor? When we examine their living conditions, they are indeed very difficult and pitiable. On the other hand, the more people who enjoy ready-made things without working, the more fulfilling their lives are. This is because of the current bad social system. We believe that the labor of masons and carpenters, in terms of value, is equal to that of engineers sitting in design offices. The police are of course serving the people, but the cleaners who empty the toilets are also fulfilling their responsibilities in the same way. Then, what should we do about our current situation? Be disappointed? Curse? Be passive? Naturally, none of these are useful. I think we only have to work harder to find a way out.

We understand that paradise is not on Mount Alps, and paradise is not in the West. Heaven and paradise exist only in our hard work. We should only use our spare time to cultivate and increase our abilities. With ability, any stubborn and unreasonable system can be broken through. We can only find happiness from the creation of our own more fulfilling career, and only this kind of happiness is true happiness! Even if we are suffering and despised by the general public now, our hard work will one day be valued丨

Paragraph, and then we will synthesize opinions to make a considerable conclusion. Now I will write this question again below:

"Standing in the position of a clerk, worker, or apprentice, how can one fulfill the obligations of a member of the Republic of China and engage in the work of resisting Japan and saving the country?" Editor's note
